< Review>
Tucked into a corner next to Main Street Market, this Taqueria offers a typical Mexican menu with good portion sizes. The burritos have been getting smaller over the last few years and they are really skimpy on the tortilla chips when you get a take out order. The nachos are to be commended as is the salsa bar. Take out orders rarely take more than 10 minutes to prepare.</Review>

We "Yelped" to Osaka after a long day of driving. The restaurant has just recently offered dine-in again! We ordered garlic edamame for an appetizer and LOVED it! All of us got beef teriyaki of one kind or another (bowl, combo, kid's). The combo came with tempura which was great (zucchini, broccoli, sweet potato, and shrimp). We enjoyed the miso soup and simple dinner salad too. Our one pause is that the beef was cooked seemingly without marinade and the teriyaki was just poured on. So, no yummy caramelized sugar! The sauce was cool but tasty, but the one or two bites missed by the drizzle weren't teriyaki. Seems easy to remedy...<//text>

< Review>
This Japanese restaurant surprised me the first time I visited. I'm always delighted when I find one that serves uni on a regular basis, usually due to shelf life and the lack of discriminating palettes it's not common on the menu of most sushi shops I have visited. The kicker is that blue fin is on the menu, another very rare commodity in your standard sushi fare. The presentation, while not the best I have seen for small shops is still quite pleasing. The staff is pleasant, sociable and friendly. Lastly, the prices are in line with most every sushi shop I have visited.< /Review>

< Review>
Course is in solid shape, and I really have to applaud the work they've done on the greens and tee boxes. Very well kept despite a lot of rain this winter.
Great price for an afternoon round, but don't expect it to be wide open. Can get a bit crowded but it's still a bargain. Driving range also available to get some swings in, but limited putting/chipping space.
Expect to get great views on #6 looking South onto the reservoir. Also don't be surprised to see deer, turkeys or even a fox/coyote.<//Review>

<username>Jeff Barber<//username><time>1508693309496</time>< Rating>
4< /Rating>
<Text>I was over from the UK for work 21/Oct/2017 and decided to bring my clubs for the weekend.  This course came up using a google maps search and had tee times listed so I thought I'd give it a punt.

The course is set in some iconic scenery.  Every hole is challenging, there is only a couple of flat holes on the course, the majority undulate and slope down the hill, which basically means that every shot has to be hit on the up slope and if you're lucky it will end up on the down side of the fairway.  Don't let this put you off this is definitely a course to practice your feet below or above the ball shots .

On one of the other reviews I read someone said that the greens were consistent.  I didn't find this, it was very much a game of two greens, wet ones and dry ones, although they had had 2 cm of rain the night before.  The one thing that they did have in common was that they were far from easy, most of the time I felt like I was playing crazy golf aiming 6 feet from the hole, miss it by an inch and the ball was 10 feet down the hill.

I played Poplar Creek the same weekend which I also reviewed and coincidentally would not play again.  All in all would I play this course again, definitely yes.</Text><pics>None<//pics><resp>None< /resp>< GmapID>

< Review>
This museum was worth the drive from Washington State to see. They have an inside museum, upstairs and down. A walk through of the outside museum was amazing to see. There's even a park behind the museum, I suggest you see that as well. I highly recommend you stop by and see if for yourself. Mr. & Mrs Jordan</Review>

<user>118426146581985919560<//user><username>cherie weller</username><Date>1522710378695</Date><Rating>4</Rating><Text>This is a small local museum that gives you a peek into life in Siskiyou County then and now. Admission is free, but help sustain the county by making the suggested donation. The museum sits next to a creek that has some beautiful open areas to walk and picnic in. Spring has arrived and there are beautiful daffodils blooming. The creek is lined with blackberry bushes (very invasive and mature vines), so watch your step if you decide to get a closer look.<//Text>< Pictures>

< text>
Amazing place! Amazing people! Amazing exhibits!
This museum is a bargain at $3 per adult and $1 under 12. Clean and friendly with impressive research library. The exhibits are diverse but focused on life in the area. Native American area on the first floor has impressive artifacts on display related to the native peoples.
The upper floor has a train set with a reproduction of the town. It also boasts an impressive and just cool collection of guns from a range of periods.
The outdoor museum is fun. Compare the rules for teachers from 1872 to the ones from 1915.
Go with your kid and support the place. I‚Äôll be there again next time I‚Äôm passing through.< /text>

<rate>4< /rate>< text>
Really casual and interesting museum. It has a lot of really nice Native American artifacts as well as a beautiful collection of antique firearms. I only give it 4 stars because there is an outdoors exhibit with original buildings from I think early I believe the mid 1800s (I'm not a historian), but it's not open year round. I went there during summer vacation and it was closed. Which I found odd. Still, it's an informative, fun, cheap way to spend an hour or two.<//text>
